A.8 What PMS-SEX Does Differently (Six Discriminators)

  1. Mechanism over motive.
    Effects are derived from configurations, not assumed inner states.
    (Α: contextual meaning = stabilization through repetition.)

  2. Cost legibility without moral escalation.
    Critique routes through Ω and Θ, not through shame, purity, humiliation, or person-rank.

  3. Non-event seriousness.
    Absence, withdrawal, silence, cancellation, delay, and hesitation can become structurally active under Λ.
    (Λ: contextual meaning = meaningful non-occurrence inside a frame.)

  4. Inner / outer / public layer discipline.
    Internal framing, outer legibility, and public circulation may diverge without canceling one another.

  5. Path-cost without pathologizing.
    Disturbance, entropy, deviation, and stabilization burden remain configuration-language only.

  6. Docking instead of fusion.
    Description and evaluation remain separated; external critique requires explicit MIP docking or another declared evaluative frame.
    (Φ: contextual meaning = recontextualization without cost erasure.)

A.9 How to Combine Lenses Without Mixing

This appendix provides a category-error firewall, not an integration recipe.

Rule 1 — Declare the active layer

Specify whether the active lens is:

  • structural description,
  • critique,
  • therapy,
  • law,
  • ethics,
  • public discourse,
  • cultural analysis,
  • phenomenology,
  • empirical reconstruction.

Do not let one layer pretend to be another.

Rule 2 — Separate claim types

PMS-SEX claim:

“In this configuration, X tends to produce Y under □/Λ/Α/Ω/Θ.”

Evaluative claim:

“Given this frame and cost layout, critique or obligation is structurally warranted / not warranted.”

Clinical claim:

“Given suffering and treatment context, this support or intervention may be appropriate.”

Legal claim:

“Given statute, evidence, and procedure, this threshold is or is not met.”

Discourse claim:

“Given publicity and circulation, this framing amplifies, distorts, or sedimentizes consequence.”

These claims may relate, but they are not interchangeable.

Rule 3 — Do not back-project

Do not back-project into PMS-SEX:

  • diagnoses,
  • motive theories,
  • moral ranks,
  • identity taxonomies,
  • legal verdicts,
  • therapeutic goals,
  • public outrage,
  • community stereotypes,
  • phenomenological claims as structural proof.

PMS-SEX reconstructs operator configurations. It does not discover inner truth.

Rule 4 — Do not let PMS-SEX overreach

PMS-SEX must not replace:

  • therapy where suffering and repair dominate,
  • law where rights, liability, and procedure dominate,
  • ethics where value commitments are explicitly being argued,
  • phenomenology where lived meaning is the object,
  • sociology where institutional history is the object,
  • public discourse analysis where circulation and audience formation are the object.

It may inform these lenses, but it should not absorb them.

Rule 5 — Use docking, not fusion

Where critique is needed, dock into MIP or another explicit evaluative frame.

Where repair is needed, switch to a clinical or support lens.

Where publicness dominates, add a discourse/media lens.

Where legal stakes dominate, use legal analysis.

Where lived meaning is decisive, use phenomenological or first-person analysis.

PMS-SEX remains the structural map, not the whole terrain.

Rule 6 — Protect dignity in language

Critique enactments, not person-worth.

Valid PMS-SEX wording:

  • “In this configuration, the enactment remains externally legible as an exposure-form.”
  • “This scene shows elevated drift potential through Ω-denial and Θ-accumulation.”
  • “Publicness sedimentizes consequences already active in the configuration.”
  • “The path-cost rises through Α-fixation and Χ-loss.”

Invalid PMS-SEX wording:

  • “This person is degraded.”
  • “This identity is disturbed.”
  • “This orientation is disordered.”
  • “This practice proves immaturity.”
  • “Public shame is justified because the outer form is legible.”

(Χ: contextual meaning = distance as maintained meta-position and stop-capability.)

A.10 Minimal Workflow

A minimal non-mixing workflow:

  1. Map the scene with PMS-SEX.
    Reconstruct frame, non-events, attractors, asymmetry, temporality, distance, integration, self-binding, outer legibility, and publicness overlays.

  2. Check the PMS entry guard.
    Preserve Χ, reversibility, and Dignity-in-Practice.

  3. Separate internal, outer, and public layers.
    Do not collapse self-description, enacted form, and public circulation.

  4. Track costs under Ω and Θ.
    Identify who carries exposure, access burdens, irreversibility, reputational risk, bodily cost, documentation, repair burden, or binding residues.

  5. Name drift only as configuration-language.
    Path-cost, disturbance, instability, or deviation remain structural.

  6. Dock only when needed.
    If public critique is required, dock into MIP.
    If suffering dominates, switch to a clinical/support lens.
    If legal thresholds matter, use legal analysis.
    If public circulation is central, add discourse/media analysis.

  7. Preserve non-capture.
    If the scene resists PMS-SEX rendering, do not force totalization. Adjacent lenses may be necessary.

(Σ: contextual meaning = holding contradiction without compensation.)

A.11 Non-Capture and Adjacent Lenses

PMS-SEX does not assume that every sexually marked configuration can be fully rendered without remainder in its own grammar.

Some scenes may require:

  • empirical reconstruction,
  • phenomenological description,
  • legal analysis,
  • medical expertise,
  • clinical support,
  • historical or cultural analysis,
  • community-specific knowledge,
  • public discourse analysis,
  • or refusal of the PMS-SEX framing altogether.

This does not weaken PMS-SEX. It prevents totalization.

Translation into PMS-SEX terms does not prove exhaustive capture. Refusal of PMS-SEX terms does not automatically indicate denial, immaturity, pathology, or drift.

PMS-SEX remains strongest where it keeps its scope: not what persons are, but what configurations do over time.

A.12 Minimal Positioning Sentence (Citable)

PMS-SEX is a praxeological scene grammar: it does not diagnose, moralize, prescribe, classify identities, or monopolize sexual meaning; it reconstructs what sexual configurations produce—especially cost layouts, drift chains, outer legibility, publicness overlays, path-cost, and exit realism—under frame, asymmetry, non-event, and time.

A.13 Short Guard Sentence (Citable)

Internal framing does not erase outer form; outer legibility does not authorize person-ranking; publicness may amplify consequence without necessarily creating it; path-cost names stabilization burden, not human worth.

Appendix B: Glossary (Δ–Ψ + Key Terms)

(Operatoric, scene-bound, citable)

This glossary defines PMS-SEX terms as structural handles, not as person labels, diagnoses, moral ranks, identity categories, or practice taxonomies.

All glossary entries are to be read under the PMS application gate:

  • Χ (Distance): maintain reflective distance and stop-capability.
  • Reversibility: keep readings scene-bound, revisable, and non-final.
  • D (Dignity-in-Practice): no shaming, humiliation, person-ranking, diagnosis, maturity ranking, or ontological evaluation.

Core PMS Operators (Δ–Ψ)

Δ — Difference
Structural distinctions that make sexual praxis legible at all: allowed/forbidden, inside/outside, self/other, private/public, local/binding-relevant, enacted/not enacted. Without Δ, no scene can form.

∇ — Impulse
Directional activation pressure arising from difference. ∇ is not motive, psychology, or moral force, but the structural fact that a configuration generates pressure that demands handling.

□ — Frame
The rule-and-role grammar that renders enactment readable and regulable: boundaries, timing, permissions, roles, publicity overlays, and what counts as inside or outside the scene. Frames constrain impulse into scenes.

Λ — Non-Event
Structurally active absence inside a frame: delay, withdrawal, silence, hesitation, cancellation, or non-occurrence under expectation. Λ can remain tolerable and non-steering, or become leverage, punishment, avoidance, or interpretive overload.

Α — Attractor
Stabilization of recurrent praxis into scripts under repetition. Α reduces friction for repetition and produces path dependence. It does not define a person; it describes the configuration’s repeated route becoming easier to repeat.

Ω — Asymmetry
Gradients of access, exposure, obligation, definitional control, exit capacity, repair burden, and cost-bearing produced by stabilized practice. Ω is structural, not moral.

Θ — Temporality
Extension of configurations into time: accumulation, irreversibility, trajectory, memory traces, documentation, bodily persistence, binding residue, and exit realism. Interpretations may change; Θ does not rewind.

Φ — Recontextualization
Embedding an existing structure into a new frame without dissolving its accumulated costs. Φ relocates meaning, narrative, or contextual interpretation; it does not by itself erase Α/Ω/Θ already made effective.

Χ — Distance
Operational stop-capability and meta-position within ongoing praxis. Χ enables interruption, hesitation, correction, non-fusion, humor, de-escalation, and outer-form awareness.

Σ — Integration
Capacity to hold and coordinate contradictions across layers without compensation, denial, splitting, or coercive simplification. Σ does not mean moral elevation; it means structural synthesis under tension.

Ψ — Self-Binding
Identity-relevant commitment over time that binds trajectories into the self-model. Ψ can be explicitly bound, explicitly suspended, kept outside a local frame, or leak covertly into frames that cannot carry binding.

Key Praxeological Terms (PMS-SEX)

Scene
A bounded enactment unit rendered legible by a frame (□) and carried through time (Θ). A scene is not reducible to intention, self-description, or public reaction.

Configuration
A concrete arrangement of operators as enacted. A configuration is not a person, not a trait, not an identity, and not a diagnosis.

Praxeological Grammar
A structural language for reading enactments, frames, asymmetries, trajectories, and self-binding without defaulting to psychology, morality, therapy, law, or person-type classification.

Drift
Predictable movement toward instability, narrowing, coercion, cost externalization, or harm when costs accumulate faster than frame, distance, integration, or binding discipline can carry them.

Viability
Structural capacity of a configuration to remain governable under Ω, Θ, and Λ without systematic D violation, exit fiction, covert Ψ leak, outer-form denial, publicness confusion, asymmetry-switch drift, parity-to-exit, or responsibility-to-authority.

Cost Layout
The patterned distribution of burdens, risks, exposure, access, repair demands, documentation, and consequences across roles and time: Ω under Θ.

Sexual Cost Topology
Scene-bound distribution of bodily, temporal, exposure-related, reputational, binding-related, exit-related, publicness-related, and responsibility-related costs across sexual role-positions. Not a score, not a person measure, not a dignity ranking.

Asymmetry-Specific Responsibility
The self-binding required of a role-position by its own cost, power, exposure, exit, and externalization profile. This is not a hierarchy of adultness; it is a scene-bound responsibility reading under Ω/Θ.

Sexual reciprocity under real asymmetry
A viability condition in sexual praxis: sexual reciprocity under real asymmetry does not require equal burdens; it requires non-externalization of unequal burdens.

Exit Realism
Whether stopping, leaving, refusing, re-reading, or redirecting remains practically available under accumulated costs. Exit realism is not a promise of rewind; it is a structural reading of remaining exit capacity under Θ.

Pseudo-Symmetry
Frame rhetoric that denies real asymmetry, rendering costs unnameable and conflict non-negotiable. Pseudo-symmetry often appears as equality language covering uneven exposure, access, after-costs, definitional control, or sexual cost topology.

EDEN/PFO Asymmetry Switch
Cross-domain reference to PMS–EDEN. In PMS-SEX, the term names the sexual instantiation of a regime-level drift: parity is claimed for autonomy, status, access, or non-binding freedom, while asymmetry is activated for protection, cost, exposure, or responsibility. Legitimate where marked and emergency-bound; drifting where unmarked, repeatable, and responsibility-shifting.

Asymmetry-Switch Drift
A drift pattern in which asymmetry is activated under real or invoked Ω/Θ pressure without being marked, bounded, and re-bound into Σ/Ψ. In PMS-SEX this is the sexual instantiation of the EDEN/PFO switch. It becomes dysfunctional where the switch is used as repeatable leverage, responsibility displacement, or unacknowledged Ψ externalization.

Parity-to-Exit
A drift pattern in which parity rhetoric is used to deny additional responsibility under unequal sexual cost topology.

Responsibility-to-Authority
A drift pattern in which required self-binding under asymmetry is converted into control, frame authority, protection entitlement, or paternalistic governance.

Sexual Drift Triad
Compact handle for the three PMS-SEX drift routes: asymmetry becomes leverage, parity becomes exit, or responsibility becomes authority.

Narrative Substitution
Use of reinterpretation (Φ) to claim resolution while structural costs, asymmetries, scripts, or temporal accumulation remain unchanged.

Frame Narrowing
Loss of alternative viable scenes; one script becomes non-substitutable. Frame narrowing is often the visible form of Α monopolization.

Drift Marker
A structural signal indicating elevated risk of destructive dynamics: Χ erosion, Θ denial, Ψ leak, Λ as steering, Ω escalation, Φ inflation, outer-form denial, publicness confusion, asymmetry-switch drift, parity-to-exit, or responsibility-to-authority.

Outer Legibility
The structurally readable action-form a scene presents under visible asymmetry, exposure, markedness, repetition, and consequence, independent of whether internal framing confirms or contests that readability. Outer legibility is not a moral verdict and not a person judgment.

Internal Framing
How a scene is inhabited, narrated, or lived from within the configuration: as play, service, devotion, experimentation, intimacy, kink, discipline, restraint, authenticity, casualness, non-binding practice, or otherwise. Internal framing may shape experience without fully determining outer structural form.

Pre-Reflective Readability
The early or immediate scene-legibility of certain marked configurations prior to elaborate internal translation or justificatory narration. This is a structural readability claim, not a psychology thesis, not a theory of innocence, and not a license for person-ranking.

Publicness as Overlay
Publicness as a frame-extension that distributes, amplifies, documents, repeats, or sedimentizes a scene’s readability and consequences without necessarily generating the scene’s primary form in the first place. Publicness modifies the consequence field; it is neither always the origin nor automatically irrelevant.

Practice Label
A name used inside or around a scene—play, kink, service, devotion, humiliation-play, discipline, experimentation, authenticity, casualness, non-binding, and so on. Practice labels may clarify internal framing, but they do not by themselves settle outer structural form.

Outer-Form Denial
A drift pattern in which internal framing, consent-language, practice labels, or later recontextualization are used to block analysis of enacted form. Outer-form denial does not prove bad faith; it marks loss of re-reading capacity.

Publicness Confusion
A drift pattern in which publicity is treated either as the whole source of consequence or as irrelevant despite amplification, documentation, circulation, reputation, or sedimentation. PMS-SEX treats publicness as overlay.

Humiliation-Form / Exposure-Form
A structurally readable action-form characterized by marked asymmetry, exposure concentration, degradation-nearness, or public/visible vulnerability. Such terms describe scene form, not person worth.

Degradation-Form
A structurally readable enactment pattern in which non-degradation under asymmetry is not preserved. The term names scene-form under D constraints, not ontological degradation of a person.

Possession-Form / Control-Form
A structurally readable action-form in which access, definition, refusal, exit, or self-binding is organized around possession-like or control-like gradients. Such terms remain configuration descriptions, not motive claims.

Authority-Form
A structurally readable action-form in which responsibility, protection, expertise, or asymmetry is converted into control, governance, or frame ownership. The term describes configuration form, not motive or person essence.

Entropic Path-Structure
A configuration’s degree of stabilization difficulty under frame, attractor formation, asymmetry, temporality, distance, integration, and self-binding. This term describes structural path-cost, not person worth, clinical status, identity rank, or moral disorder.

Neutral Disturbance
A strictly structural term for deviation, perturbation, instability, or added stabilization burden within a configuration. It does not imply moral failure, diagnosis, pathology, lower dignity, or degraded personhood.

Path-Cost
The operator-work required for a configuration to remain coherent, reversible, non-coercive, and dignity-preserving over time. Path-cost may rise through Λ-density, Α-fixation, Ω-asymmetry, Θ-accumulation, Χ-loss, failed or overloaded Σ, covert Ψ leak, outer-form denial, visible-form fixation, publicness sedimentation, category monopolization, access entitlement drift, body/boundary person-truth drift, after-scene dignity failure, sexed leniency drift, asymmetric self-control burden, boundary-aggression collapse, asymmetry-switch drift, parity-to-exit, or responsibility-to-authority. Path-cost is configuration-language only.

Stabilization Burden
The amount of framing, distance, integration, self-binding discipline, or cost accounting required to keep a configuration from narrowing, externalizing costs, or collapsing under recurrence.

Configuration-Level Deviation
A structural divergence from a lower-cost or more strongly stabilized path. It applies to scene organization and operator dynamics, not to persons, identities, orientations, or ontological status.

Non-Capture
The possibility that a sexually marked configuration may not be fully rendered without remainder in PMS-SEX grammar. Non-capture protects PMS-SEX from totalization; refusal of PMS-SEX terms does not automatically indicate denial, immaturity, pathology, or drift.

Sexed Cost Topology and Drift Overlay Terms

The following terms are PMS-SEX overlay terms. They are not PMS operators, not diagnoses, not person labels, not sex truths, not moral ranks, and not practical instructions. They name scene-bound configuration profiles only.

Biological Affordance Without Destiny
A scene-bound reading of biological structure as affordance rather than fate: bodies, risks, thresholds, asymmetries, costs, and likely strategy spaces may matter without coding completed conduct, moral rank, role proof, person truth, hierarchy, or destiny.

  • Status: overlay term; is_operator: false.
  • Operators: Δ / Ω / Θ / □.
  • Guard: biology is not destiny; biological nearness means tendency, not value; tendency means starting condition, not endpoint; starting condition means learning demand, not inferiority.

Concept Human / Sexed Dependency
The anthropological claim that human life is not self-originating but emerges through sexually differentiated bodily and social conditions: birth, reproduction, dependency, care, embodiment, vulnerability, kinship, and intergenerational continuity.

  • Status: overlay term; is_operator: false.
  • Operators: Δ / Ω / Θ / Ψ.
  • Guard: sexed dependency is not heterosexual mandate, cis-normative hierarchy, partner prescription, reproductive command, orientation ranking, or person incompleteness.

Unlearned Handling / Unvermittelter Umgang
A configuration in which real sexual impulse must be managed under contradictory, moralized, or non-operational frame rules, producing clumsiness, avoidance, overcorrection, simulation, or access-threshold drift.

  • Status: overlay term; is_operator: false.
  • Operators: ∇ / □ / Λ / Α / Χ.
  • Guard: unlearned handling can explain clumsiness without excusing cost externalization. It is not male innocence by default, not excuse for coercion, not entitlement, and not denial of risk.

Direct Otherness
The reality-correction condition of sexual adultization: a role-position encounters an other who can respond, refuse, invite, misunderstand, correct, desire, withdraw, and remain non-identical with the script.

  • Status: overlay term; is_operator: false.
  • Operators: Δ / □ / Ω / Χ / Σ / Ψ.
  • Guard: direct otherness is not access entitlement. No person owes access, body, affection, labor, explanation, correction, or availability.

Sacralized Genital Self-Reading
A configuration in which the genital is treated as identity oracle, altar, proof, shame-center, liberation symbol, victim center, potency evidence, boundary mystery, or immunity source.

  • Status: overlay term; is_operator: false.
  • Operators: Δ / □ / Φ / Α / Ω / Θ / Χ.
  • Guard: genital meaning is real; genital sovereignty is drift. The term does not criticize genital awareness, body literacy, pleasure, vulnerability, shame recovery, or embodied self-knowledge.

Genital Emancipation
The integration of genitality without denial and without enthronement. The genital is carried as real—impulse, access, boundary, shame, potency, vulnerability, pleasure, bodily consequence, and reproductive possibility may matter—without becoming command, altar, proof, confession, identity oracle, shame-center, or immunity source.

  • Status: overlay term; is_operator: false.
  • Operators: Χ / Σ / Ψ / D.
  • Guard: not anti-sex, not anti-body, not anti-pleasure, not purity rhetoric, not de-eroticization, not moral ranking, and not therapeutic instruction.

Adult Sexual Emancipation
The configuration capability in which genitality is integrated without becoming sovereign. It is not increased enactment, public confession, boundary reduction, genital celebration, visibility alone, or sacralized self-description.

  • Status: overlay term; is_operator: false.
  • Operators: Χ / Σ / Ψ / D.
  • Guard: not a person rank, not a maturity score, not a dignity status, not an orientation hierarchy. Adult Sexual Emancipation is the capacity to carry one’s sexual body under Χ, Σ, and Ψ without denial, enthronement, or externalization.

Ambivalence-Withdrawal / Love-Ending Drift
A configuration in which love, attachment, or sexual-relational binding weakens because the resonance field no longer stabilizes desire, safety, determination, or future-readability. Withdrawal may then appear as the end of love.

  • Status: drift overlay; is_operator: false.
  • Operators: Λ / Α / Ω / Θ / Ψ.
  • Guard: not female essence, not blame, not fickleness by nature, not proof that women cannot bind. It names one possible role-position drift where ambiguity remains mobile and no longer self-binds into the prior scene.

Post-Access Withdrawal
A configuration in which access-threshold pressure resolves through enactment while Ψ does not bind to the after-scene. The role-position withdraws after access has been achieved.

  • Status: drift overlay; is_operator: false.
  • Operators: ∇ / Α / Ω / Θ / Ψ.
  • Guard: not male essence, not proof of bad intent, not automatic exploitation, not proof that male desire cannot bind. It names one possible role-position drift where access resolution reduces the pressure that had previously simulated binding.

Covert Ψ-Expectation
A binding expectation that becomes structurally active without being explicitly carried by the frame: care, access, ambiguity, desire, repetition, or after-scene conduct creates binding relevance while the frame still narrates non-binding.

  • Status: overlay term; is_operator: false.
  • Operators: Λ / Α / Ω / Θ / Ψ.
  • Guard: non-binding language does not erase structured expectation where a scene induced, used, allowed, or benefited from Ψ-expectation. No automatic guilt; no automatic exculpation.

Public Measure-Formation
Sexual praxis produces public measures where it structures costs, consent, consequence, binding, dignity, risk, responsibility, law, or long-term effects.

  • Status: overlay term; is_operator: false.
  • Operators: □ / Ω / Θ / D.
  • Guard: public measure does not imply public confession. Preference remains private until it structures a concrete scene.

Confession Regime
A false transparency regime in which sexual preference, fantasy, arousal, or self-description is pressured into public inventory and then treated as person truth.

  • Status: overlay term; is_operator: false.
  • Operators: □ / Φ / Χ / Ψ.
  • Guard: no preference-to-person collapse; no confession mandate; no identity ranking.

Δ-Density at the Body
A dense concentration of symbolic and praxeological switching points at the body: boundary, visibility, shame, exposure, availability, recognition, bodily consequence, and transformation.

  • Status: overlay term; is_operator: false.
  • Operators: Δ / □ / Ω / Θ.
  • Guard: scene-bound; not female essence; not sex truth; not dignity ranking.

Body-Switching Point / Körper-Schaltstelle
A role-position in which small changes in body-state, boundary, exposure, shame, recognition, or availability produce large changes in scene meaning.

  • Status: overlay term; is_operator: false.
  • Operators: Δ / □ / Ω / Θ / Φ.
  • Guard: role-position term only; no biology-as-destiny; no person typing.

Body/Boundary Coding
A configuration in which body-state, exposure, withholding, opening, refusal, shame, recognition, or boundary-form becomes a central readability channel of the scene.

  • Status: overlay term; is_operator: false.
  • Operators: Δ / □ / Ω / Θ.
  • Guard: body/boundary coding remains scene-bound; it must not become person truth.

Body/Boundary Coding Deviance
A drift path in which body/boundary coding stabilizes into category, repetition, visibility, permission-image, or person-truth pressure.

  • Status: drift overlay; is_operator: false.
  • Operators: Δ / Α / Ω / Θ / Χ.
  • Guard: not female essence, not pathology, not moral rank, not sex truth.

Access-Based Deviance
A drift path in which sexual difference becomes legible through thresholds of access: what can be reached, expanded, exceeded, earned, purchased, simulated, or imagined as available.

  • Status: drift overlay; is_operator: false.
  • Operators: Δ / Α / Ω / Θ / Χ.
  • Guard: access is threshold-language, not entitlement. No person owes access.

Permission-Image
A symbolic, pornographic, or scene-bound image in which a category appears to carry permission, invitation, counterdesire, or authorization within itself.

  • Status: overlay term; is_operator: false.
  • Operators: □ / Φ / Α / Ω.
  • Guard: permission-image is not consent, not encounter, and not concrete correction by a real other.

Simulated Counterdesire
A mediated or imagined form in which the other appears to want, invite, require, or authorize the category, without concrete correction by an actual other.

  • Status: overlay term; is_operator: false.
  • Operators: Φ / Α / Ω / Θ.
  • Guard: not evidence of actual desire; not consent; not entitlement.

Access/Counterdesire Loop
A drift loop in which limited real access, simulated counterdesire, permission-images, and repeatable category availability stabilize a route where the image replaces encounter.

  • Status: drift overlay; is_operator: false.
  • Operators: Δ / □ / Α / Ω / Θ / Χ.
  • Guard: configuration-language only; no psychology of men; no entitlement; no person diagnosis.

Category Monopolization
A drift pattern in which category availability replaces frame breadth: what is searchable, repeatable, combinable, or easy to re-enter becomes easier than re-reading the broader scene.

  • Status: drift overlay; is_operator: false.
  • Operators: Δ / Α / Θ / Χ.
  • Guard: category pressure is not person truth, orientation taxonomy, or pathology.

Access Entitlement Drift
A drift pattern in which access language becomes claim language: refusal, delay, distance, or non-availability is treated as injury, deprivation, or illegitimate withholding.

  • Status: drift overlay; is_operator: false.
  • Operators: Ω / Λ / Θ / Χ.
  • Guard: access remains threshold-language; no entitlement; no coercion authorization.

Body/Boundary Person-Truth Drift
A drift pattern in which body-state, exposure, shame, recognition, availability, or boundary-form is treated as the truth of a person.

  • Status: drift overlay; is_operator: false.
  • Operators: Δ / Ω / Θ / Φ / Χ.
  • Guard: no person truth; no sex truth; no dignity ranking.

After-Scene Dignity / Nachher-Würde
A Dignity-in-Practice criterion under Θ carryover: whether a scene remains carryable afterward without person-shrinking, shame residue, blame reversal, immunity, degradation, or self-worth leakage.

  • Status: D/Θ overlay; is_operator: false.
  • Operators: D / Θ / Χ / Σ / Ψ.
  • Guard: not a feeling-test, not moral purity, not retrospective punishment; it is a temporal dignity criterion.

Positive Dominance / Guided Dominance
A bounded configuration in which guided intensity, holding, leading, opening, or negotiated boundary-nearness may be sought without reducing the person to the scene.

  • Status: practice-form overlay; is_operator: false.
  • Operators: Ω / Χ / Σ / Ψ / D.
  • Guard: dominance-nearness is not automatically indignity; it becomes drift where Χ, Σ, Ψ, or after-scene dignity fail. No violence authorization.

Visible-Form Fixation
A drift pattern in which the most visible action-form is treated as the whole structure, while frame history, Λ pressure, Ω/Θ cost topology, internal framing, category formation, and temporal accumulation are under-read.

  • Status: drift overlay; is_operator: false.
  • Operators: □ / Ω / Θ / Χ.
  • Guard: visible form matters, but it does not exhaust the scene; no person verdict.

Humiliation-to-Control-Collapse Corridor
A drift corridor in which repeated humiliation-near, degradation-near, shame-near, or exposure-near marking overloads Χ/Ψ until stop-capability, self-binding, distance, or meta-position become unstable.

  • Status: drift overlay; is_operator: false.
  • Operators: Ω / Θ / Χ / Ψ / D.
  • Guard: no threshold rule, no violence justification, no retaliation logic, no practical instruction.

Sexed Leniency Drift
A drift pattern in which leniency, exception, blame, relief, or contextualization tracks sex-coded readability rather than scene, cost, capacity, responsibility, and actual operator load.

  • Status: drift overlay; is_operator: false.
  • Operators: Ω / R / Ψ / D.
  • Guard: not a claim about men or women; no sex truth; leniency must remain configuration-bound.

Asymmetric Self-Control Burden
A drift pattern in which one role-position must carry disproportionate restraint, de-escalation, non-reaction, interruption discipline, distance, or self-binding, while another role-position’s escalation is more easily contextualized.

  • Status: drift overlay; is_operator: false.
  • Operators: Χ / Ψ / Ω / D.
  • Guard: higher Χ/Ψ burden requires higher dignity recognition, not lower recognition. No person blame.

Boundary-Aggression Collapse
A drift pattern in which stopping, refusal, withdrawal, resistance, boundary-setting, or distance creation is too quickly read as aggression — or aggression, punishment, retaliation, discharge, or escalation is framed as mere boundary-setting.

  • Status: drift overlay; is_operator: false.
  • Operators: Χ / Ω / Θ / D.
  • Guard: does not adjudicate concrete cases; does not authorize response, force, retaliation, or moral verdict.

Dignity and Critique Terms

D — Dignity-in-Practice
Enacted restraint and non-degradation within a frame under asymmetry. D is a constraint on how practice occurs, not a status of persons and not a metaphysical dignity claim.

D-Compliance
The degree to which a configuration preserves D as an enactment constraint: asymmetry is governed, stopping remains usable, meaning does not leak covertly across frame boundaries, and critique does not become humiliation.

D-Violation
A configuration-level failure to preserve non-degradation under asymmetry. D-violation does not lower a person’s dignity; it identifies failure in enacted handling.

Ψ Leak
Covert introduction of meaning, possession, identity proof, self-worth, or commitment demand into a frame that cannot explicitly carry binding.

Ω Escalation
Use of asymmetry as a steering mechanism rather than a governed layout: access pressure, boundary testing, definitional control, cost shifting, or uneven exit capacity becoming normal inside the frame.

Χ Loss
Collapse of stop-capability and meta-position; critique, hesitation, refusal, humor, de-escalation, or outer-form awareness become socially or practically unavailable.

Φ Inflation
Repeated recontextualization that claims resolution while Α/Ω/Θ remain unchanged. Φ inflation often substitutes narrative repair for integration (Σ).

Α Fixation
Attractor stabilization becoming monopolizing: one script becomes non-substitutable, alternatives lose practical legibility, and repetition replaces choice.

Θ Overload
Accumulated costs exceed frame capacity. Exit fictions persist until collapse becomes abrupt or expensive.

Cost-Topology Mismatch
A configuration-level mismatch between declared parity, autonomy, non-binding status, or mutuality and the actual distribution of bodily, reputational, exposure-related, publicness-related, exit-related, or responsibility-related costs.

Unmarked Ω Activation
Asymmetry activation that is not explicitly marked as exceptional, necessary, bounded, or re-bound into Σ/Ψ. This is a drift marker, not a person label.

Ψ Externalization
Displacement of self-binding onto another role-position: the other must carry, prove, repair, endure, or absorb costs that should be handled as role-specific self-binding.

MIP Docking Terms

MIP Docking
Optional evaluative interface between PMS-SEX and Maturity in Practice. PMS-SEX describes operator profiles; MIP asks when critique is legitimate. Docking changes the critique lens, not the PMS-SEX operator grammar.

Operator Profile Only
A PMS-SEX discipline rule: unmarked Ω activation, weak Χ, missing Σ, Ψ externalization, biological-affordance pressure, sexed-dependency framing, unlearned handling, direct-otherness failure, sacralized genital self-reading, genital-sovereignty drift, failed genital emancipation, ambivalence-withdrawal, post-access withdrawal, covert Ψ-expectation, category monopolization, access entitlement drift, body/boundary person-truth drift, after-scene dignity failure, visible-form fixation, sexed leniency drift, asymmetric self-control burden, boundary-aggression collapse, parity-to-exit, responsibility-to-authority, and cost-topology mismatch are recorded as structural profiles, not as direct person-adultness, maturity, dignity, orientation, sex, genital, or worth verdicts.

Maturity-Relevant Evaluation
Evaluation that belongs only to the MIP docking layer. It must remain scene-bound, reversible, non-person-ranking, non-diagnostic, and D-preserving.

Asymmetry-Specific Self-Binding
MIP-compatible question asking whether a role-position carries the self-binding required by its cost, power, exposure, exit, and externalization profile. It must not become an essence claim or dignity hierarchy.

Methodological Guards

Scene-Bound
Claims apply only to the described configuration, not to persons globally.

Reversibility (Interpretive)
Descriptions remain revisable; consequences under Θ do not rewind through reinterpretation.

Non-Diagnostic
No inference about pathology, motive structure, mental state, clinical condition, or psychological essence.

Non-Moralizing
No purity claims, virtue ranking, moral ontology, person-worth judgment, identity hierarchy, maturity hierarchy, or humiliation.

Non-Prescriptive
No how-to, optimization, intervention method, risk-management manual, or instruction for enactment.

No Person-Typing
PMS-SEX terms describe configurations, not character, essence, sexual identity, orientation, maturity level, or personal worth.

No Orientation Taxonomy
Default/deviation, entropy, disturbance, and path-cost language must not be converted into a sexual-orientation classification or hierarchy.

No Public-Punishment Inference
Outer legibility does not automatically authorize public critique, exposure, shaming, or attribution escalation. Public critique requires a separate evaluative docking lens.

No Direct Adultness Verdict
PMS-SEX may record operator profiles and drift markers. It may not directly evaluate person-adultness. Adultness-relevant critique belongs to MIP docking and must remain scene-bound, reversible, non-person-ranking, and D-preserving.

Internal / Outer / Public Separation
Internal framing, outer legibility, and public circulation may overlap, but must not be collapsed into one another.

Final Path-Cost Guard
Disturbance, entropy, deviation, drift, inadultness, failed emancipation, and path-cost language name structural stabilization burden, not human worth, identity rank, orientation status, maturity level, adultness, dignity status, sex truth, genital truth, biological destiny, or clinical disorder. Biological-affordance, sexed-dependency, impulse-nearness, unlearned-handling, direct-otherness, category, access, body/boundary, genital, after-scene dignity, withdrawal, self-control burden, sexed leniency, and boundary/aggression terms remain configuration-language only and do not create new operators.

Appendix C: Operator Table

(Canonical order, dependencies, typical drift markers)

This table summarizes the Δ–Ψ operator spine as used in PMS-SEX.

It specifies dependencies, minimal praxeological function, and typical drift markers when an operator is denied, overloaded, rhetorically bypassed, or made to carry more than its position in the chain can support.

The table is descriptive, not normative.

It does not add operators, revise PMS v1.3, convert derived PMS-SEX terms into base meta-axioms, or turn drift markers into person labels.

C.1 Canonical Operator Table (Δ–Ψ)

Operator Name Depends on Minimal praxeological function Typical drift markers (non-exhaustive)
Δ Difference — Creates distinctions that make sexual praxis legible at all: inside/outside, allowed/forbidden, self/other, private/public, local/binding-relevant. Undifferentiated pressure; fusion; illegibility of boundaries; inability to name what differs.
∇ Impulse Δ Introduces directional pressure that demands handling: activation, pull, movement toward or away from a difference. Escalation without framing; pressure outruns coordination; urgency becomes self-justifying.
□ Frame Δ, ∇ Constrains impulse into a readable scene grammar: roles, rules, permissions, timing, publicity overlays, and what counts as inside/outside. Ambiguity drift; retroactive rule changes; practice labels replacing frame analysis; mono-frame dominance; outer-form denial.
Λ Non-Event □ Makes absence, delay, silence, hesitation, cancellation, and withdrawal structurally active under expectation. Silence as leverage; withdrawal as punishment; chronic “maybe/later”; interpretive overload; non-occurrence becomes steering.
Α Attractor Δ, ∇, □, Λ Stabilizes recurrent scripts under repetition; produces path dependence and lower-friction repeatability. Script monopolization; loss of alternatives; repetition replaces choice; practice becomes non-substitutable; label capture protects the route.
Ω Asymmetry Α Produces gradients of access, exposure, obligation, definitional control, exit margin, repair burden, and cost-bearing. Pseudo-symmetry; covert cost shifting; exposure concentration; power as steering variable; asymmetry moralized instead of regulated.
Θ Temporality Ω, Α Extends configurations into trajectories: accumulation, irreversibility, memory traces, documentation, bodily persistence, and exit realism. Exit fiction; delayed collapse; persistence despite visible costs; public sedimentation; recontextualization claims rewind.
Φ Recontextualization Θ, Ω, □ Relocates an existing structure into a new frame without dissolving costs already active under Α/Ω/Θ. Narrative substitution; “it is different now” resets; cost denial; inner re-description used to erase outer form.
Χ Distance Φ, Θ, □ Enables stop-capability and meta-position within ongoing praxis: pause, refusal, humor, re-reading, de-escalation, non-fusion. Stop punished; critique read as betrayal; outer-form awareness forbidden; escalation lock-in; loss of self-correction.
Σ Integration Χ, Φ Synthesizes contradictions without compensation, denial, splitting, or coercive simplification. Fragmentation; Φ substitutes for Σ; Α/Ω/Λ compensate for unresolved contradiction; split coherence.
Ψ Self-Binding Σ, Θ, Χ Binds integrated trajectories into identity-relevant commitments over time. Ψ leak; possession or self-worth claims smuggled into limited frames; identity capture; local enactment becomes proof demand.

C.2 Reading Notes (Formal)

1. Dependencies are strict.
An operator cannot function coherently if its predecessors are structurally absent. Apparent “shortcuts” typically signal compensation drift, rhetorical bypass, or domain-specific shorthand that must be translated back into the canonical Δ–Ψ path.

2. Drift markers are not diagnoses.
They are predictable configuration effects when load exceeds regulation capacity or when an operator is denied rhetorically but operative in fact. Drift markers do not name persons, motives, pathologies, identities, or worth.

3. □ does not collapse into labels.
Frame labels and internal naming do not by themselves settle the full outer legibility of enacted form. A scene can be internally named as play, consent, service, devotion, or authenticity while still requiring analysis of asymmetry, exposure, markedness, temporality, and cost layout.

4. Λ is not nothing.
Non-events are structurally active when they occur under expectation. Silence, withdrawal, delay, hesitation, or cancellation may remain tolerable, but they may also become steering variables.

5. Α is not essence.
Attractor formation describes path stabilization, not personal nature. A repeated route becoming easier to repeat does not define what a person is.

6. Ω is structural, not moral.
Asymmetry names gradients of access, exposure, capacity, obligation, or cost-bearing. Naming Ω does not assign blame, rank persons, or deny consent; it reconstructs where leverage and burden appear.

7. Θ does not rewind.
Interpretations may be revised, but accumulated consequences do not disappear through later narrative change. Memory traces, documentation, bodily effects, reputational exposure, and binding residues remain Θ-relevant.

8. Φ is never curative by itself.
Recontextualization may alter how a scene is narrated or inhabited, but it does not by itself erase the outer form that has already become structurally effective under Θ. Persistent Φ without Χ/Σ increases drift risk.

9. Χ is the decisive application-side limiter.
Across PMS-SEX, loss of distance reliably predicts escalation, fixation, delayed collapse, and outer-form denial. Χ is not purity or superiority; it is stop-capability and meta-position.

10. Σ cannot be forced.
Integration is reachable only where contradictions can be held without collapse, compensation, or coercive simplification. Forced synthesis often masks Φ inflation or Α fixation.

11. Ψ can bind, suspend, or leak.
Self-binding may be explicit, deliberately suspended as an attribution condition, or covertly operative as leak. Suspension is not removal from the PMS chain; it is a domain-specific boundary condition inside a configuration.

12. Publicness is an overlay.
Publicness may distribute, amplify, document, repeat, or sedimentize outer legibility and consequence. It does not necessarily generate the primary action-form.

13. Path-cost remains configuration-language.
Higher path-cost or stabilization burden describes operator-work under recurrence and temporality. It does not imply person-ranking, diagnosis, moral disorder, lower dignity, or sexual-orientation taxonomy.

C.3 Cross-Reference Map (Orientation)

  • Ch. 0: Scope, PMS operator spine, entry guard, scene binding, internal/outer/public distinction, biological affordance, sexed dependency, overlay discipline, MIP separation, and project-wide misreading guards.
  • Ch. 1: Sexuality is established as recurring praxis pressure under Δ/∇/□, with preference kept distinct from praxis until it structures a scene.
  • Ch. 2: Drive is treated as structural pressure, not inner motive; impulse-nearness is distinguished from malice without erasing consequence.
  • Ch. 3: Frame logic shows why situation, enacted form, and outer legibility cannot be settled by intention or later re-description alone; unlearned handling is introduced as a frame problem.
  • Ch. 4: Asymmetry becomes the sexual cost topology: unequal burdens are readable without becoming person rank, sex truth, or moral verdict.
  • Ch. 5: Temporality turns episodes into trajectories; category escalation, ambivalence-withdrawal, post-access withdrawal, and covert Ψ-expectation become readable under Θ/Ψ.
  • Ch. 6: Exit realism clarifies that leaving redirects a trajectory without rewinding accumulated costs, category fixation, body/boundary overhang, or after-scene dignity burden.
  • Ch. 7: Non-event logic shows how absence, delay, withdrawal, and indeterminacy can become scene-active under expectation without becoming automatic blame.
  • Ch. 8: Pattern formation explains how repeated handling and category availability stabilize into attractors without becoming person essence.
  • Ch. 9: Recontextualization changes where pressure works, but does not erase prior costs or outer form already effective under Θ.
  • Ch. 10: Distance is the governability operator: stop-capability, boundary readability, and meta-position without purity, superiority, or response authorization.
  • Ch. 11: Integration is a capacity, not an obligation; it becomes relevant where contradictions can no longer be carried by local handling alone.
  • Ch. 12: Self-binding marks the threshold where scenes become attribution-relevant across time; Ψ leak and covert Ψ-expectation name binding mismatch without person verdict.
  • Ch. 13: The body and the real other appear as non-operator remainders: material consequence and direct otherness limit image, category, fantasy, and self-description.
  • Ch. 14: Modulators describe domain-specific operator weightings without typing people, psychologizing motives, or making path-likelihood into destiny.
  • Ch. 15: Deviance is treated as consequence structure and category formation, not person-type, defect, diagnosis, sex truth, or moral pathology.
  • Ch. 16: High intensity becomes risky through intensity–structure mismatch, not because intensity is morally bad.
  • Ch. 17: Suspended Ψ is treated as a boundary condition, not as removal of self-binding from the PMS chain.
  • Ch. 18: Dysfunctional dynamics track drift chains under Λ/Α/Ω/Θ, Χ erosion, Ψ leak, boundary-aggression collapse, visible-form fixation, and asymmetry-switch drift.
  • Ch. 19: Viability criteria specify minimum governability under Ω, Θ, Χ, Ψ handling, cost topology, after-scene dignity, and publicness proportion.
  • Ch. 20: Minimal psychology functions only as a structural self-check when drift dynamics and viability criteria are already visible but not self-correcting.
  • Ch. 21: Dignity-in-Practice constrains Ω use, Χ availability, after-scene dignity, boundary/aggression readability, and non-humiliating critique.
  • Ch. 22: MIP docks evaluative critique onto PMS-SEX operator profiles without layer mixing or direct adultness/person verdict.
  • Ch. 23: Limits preserve non-capture, prevent psychology/taxonomy/therapy/political-program drift, and keep entropy/path-cost language scope-bound.
  • Ch. 24: The conclusion consolidates the closing axis: biology without destiny, dependency without mandate, impulse without malice-collapse, otherness without entitlement, genitality without sovereignty, and Adult Sexual Emancipation.

C.4 Inner / Outer / Public Reading Note

A scene may be:

  • internally framed one way,
  • externally readable another way,
  • publicly circulated in a third way,
  • and temporally carried in a fourth way.

PMS-SEX does not collapse these layers. It reconstructs how frame, markedness, asymmetry, publicness, and consequence interact without allowing internal naming or public amplification to erase enacted form.

C.5 Path-Cost / Disturbance Guard

Where the table refers to instability, disturbance, deviation, entropy, higher path-cost, or drift overlay markers, these terms apply only to configuration dynamics.

They describe stabilization burden under the Δ–Ψ grammar, not person status, identity rank, orientation taxonomy, clinical disorder, moral failure, maturity level, adultness, dignity status, or degraded dignity.

This also applies to PMS-SEX overlay terms: biological-affordance pressure, sexed-dependency framing, unlearned handling, direct-otherness failure, category pressure, access thresholds, body/boundary coding, sacralized genital self-reading, genital-sovereignty drift, ambivalence-withdrawal, post-access withdrawal, covert Ψ-expectation, after-scene dignity burden, visible-form fixation, sexed leniency drift, asymmetric self-control burden, and boundary-aggression collapse. They are reduced signatures of configuration load, not new operators, not person measures, not sex truths, not genital truths, not maturity scores, and not orientation taxonomies.

Final guard: Disturbance-language is admissible only as configuration-language. The moment it becomes person-language, diagnosis, rank, orientation taxonomy, maturity hierarchy, dignity hierarchy, sex truth, violence authorization, or humiliation, it leaves PMS-SEX.

C.6 Minimal Table Sentence (Citable)

In PMS-SEX, drift is not explained by motives but by operator overloads and denials: when frames narrow, non-events steer, attractors monopolize, asymmetries distribute costs unevenly, and temporality accumulates faster than distance can regulate.

Appendix D: One-Page Structural Map

Δ → Ψ as a Praxeological Flowchart (Θ / Ω / Λ highlighted)

(Orientation map, not an explanatory text)

This map is a compressed orientation aid. It does not add operators, revise PMS v1.3, classify persons, diagnose motives, prescribe actions, or replace the chapter-level analyses.

D.1 Reading Instruction (One Sentence)

This map shows how sexual practice becomes structured over time: from difference and impulse, through framing and non-events, into stabilized paths, asymmetry layouts, temporal costs, recontextualization, distance, integration, and self-binding—unless distance interrupts drift early enough.

D.2 Linear Spine (Canonical Flow)

Δ → ∇ → □ → Λ → Α → Ω → Θ → Φ → Χ → Σ → Ψ

This is the canonical PMS v1.3 spine.

All arrows are directional and dependency-bound. PMS-SEX uses this sequence as a domain-specific application path; it does not rename, reorder, or replace the PMS operators.

D.3 Structural Zones (Compressed)

ZONE 1 — Activation & Legibility

(What makes praxis possible at all)

Δ (Difference)
   ↓
∇ (Impulse)
   ↓
□ (Frame)
  • Δ creates distinctions: inside/outside, allowed/forbidden, private/public, local/binding-relevant.
  • ∇ introduces pressure that demands handling.
  • □ constrains pressure into a readable scene grammar: roles, rules, timing, permissions, boundaries, and overlays.

Failure mode:
→ pressure without legibility → escalation, fusion, ambiguity drift, or retroactive rule-making.

Reading note:
Frame labels and internal naming do not by themselves settle the full outer legibility of enacted form.

ZONE 2 — Absence, Repetition, Stabilization

(Where drift begins to form)

□
 ↓
Λ (Non-Event)
 ↓
Α (Attractor)
  • Λ activates absence, delay, silence, hesitation, withdrawal, or cancellation under expectation.
  • Α stabilizes repetition into scripts, lower-friction routes, and path dependence.

Key insight:
Absence is not neutral; repetition is not free.

Failure mode:
→ Λ becomes steering; Α becomes monopolizing; the scene narrows before it appears dramatic.

ZONE 3 — COST AXIS (Core of PMS-SEX)

(Always active once Α exists)

Α
 ↓
Ω (Asymmetry)
 ↓
Θ (Temporality)

This is the irreversible cost axis.

  • Ω distributes access, exposure, obligation, definitional control, exit capacity, repair burden, and cost-bearing.
  • Θ extends configurations into trajectories: repetition, accumulation, irreversibility, memory traces, documentation, bodily persistence, and exit realism.

Nothing after this point is consequence-free.
Interpretations may change; Θ does not rewind.

Failure mode:
→ asymmetry becomes steering; costs are externalized; exit fiction replaces exit realism.

ZONE 4 — Narrative Handling (Ambivalent)

Θ / Ω / □
      ↓
Φ (Recontextualization)
  • Φ relocates an existing structure into a new frame.
  • Costs, asymmetries, scripts, and temporal residues travel with it unless explicitly carried.

Bifurcation:

Φ + Χ → possible regulation / re-reading
Φ without Χ → narrative substitution drift

Reading note:
Recontextualization may alter how a scene is narrated or inhabited, but it does not by itself erase the outer form that has already become structurally effective under Θ.

ZONE 5 — Regulation vs. Drift

Φ / Θ / □
      ↓
Χ (Distance)
  • Χ enables stop-capability and meta-position inside the running configuration.
  • Χ includes interruption, hesitation, refusal, humor, de-escalation, re-reading, and outer-form awareness.

Decisive split:

Χ operative                 Χ eroded
     ↓                          ↓
re-reading / regulation      escalation / fixation / delayed collapse

Χ loss is one of the strongest drift predictors in PMS-SEX because it removes the configuration’s capacity to interrupt itself before Α and Θ harden.

ZONE 6 — Coherence Handling

Χ
 ↓
Σ (Integration)
  • Σ holds contradictions without coercion, denial, splitting, or compensation.
  • Σ is not moral elevation; it is the capacity to coordinate multiple layers without collapse.

If Σ fails:
→ substitutes take over: Α repetition, Φ inflation, Ω control, Λ withdrawal, or Ψ leak.

ZONE 7 — Identity-Relevant Binding

Σ + Θ + Χ
     ↓
Ψ (Self-Binding)
  • Ψ binds trajectories into identity-relevant commitments over time.
  • Ψ can be explicitly bound, deliberately suspended as an attribution condition, kept outside a local frame, or leak covertly.

Ψ leak = high-risk drift condition:
binding pressure enters frames that cannot explicitly carry binding.

Reading note:
Suspension of Ψ is not removal from the PMS chain. It is a domain-specific boundary condition inside a configuration.

D.4 Highlighted Drift Corridors (Overlay)

Primary destructive chain

Ψ leak
 → Ω escalation
 → Χ loss
 → Α fixation
 → Θ overload
 → exit collapse

Reading:
Once meaning and attribution become covert, asymmetry more easily becomes a steering variable. When distance is not operative, the script hardens, and temporal costs accumulate until the exit fiction breaks.

Non-event / attractor chain

Λ density
 → Α monopolization
 → Ω as steering
 → Θ accumulation
 → Χ collapse
 → late Ψ capture

Reading:
Repeated absence, delay, withholding, or non-occurrence can become structurally active before explicit conflict appears. Collapse is usually delayed, not sudden.

Label / outer-form denial chain

practice-label capture
 → outer-form denial
 → publicness confusion
 → delayed cost recognition

Reading:
Internal labels may settle the internal story while enacted form remains structurally readable. Public reaction is then treated either as the whole problem or as irrelevant, preventing the configuration from seeing how publicness may amplify readability without creating it.

D.4a Drift Overlay Markers (Non-Operators)

The following overlays are reduced signatures, not dependency claims. They do not add, remove, rename, or reorder PMS operators. They mark where the canonical Δ→Ψ spine becomes especially burdened in PMS-SEX configurations.

biological affordance / sexed dependency / impulse-nearness
   ↓
category pressure / access thresholds / body-boundary coding / genital self-reading
   ↓
category monopolization / access entitlement / body-boundary person-truth / genital sovereignty
   ↓
after-scene dignity burden / covert Ψ-expectation / self-control burden / boundary-aggression readability

Overlay list:

  • biological-affordance pressure: embodied risks, thresholds, asymmetries, or strategy spaces structure the scene without determining destiny.
  • sexed-dependency framing: human emergence and dependency become scene-relevant without becoming relationship mandate.
  • unlearned handling: impulse must be managed under contradictory or non-operational frame rules.
  • direct-otherness failure: image, category, fantasy, or self-reading replaces correction by a real other.
  • visible-form fixation: visible action-form is read as the whole configuration.
  • category monopolization: category availability replaces frame breadth.
  • access entitlement drift: access thresholds become claim language.
  • body/boundary person-truth drift: body-state or boundary-form becomes person truth.
  • sacralized genital self-reading: genital meaning becomes identity oracle, proof, altar, shame-center, liberation symbol, or immunity source.
  • genital-sovereignty drift: the genital governs the person or scene rather than being integrated under Χ/Σ/Ψ.
  • ambivalence-withdrawal: ambiguity resolves as withdrawal where resonance, safety, determination, or future-readability no longer bind.
  • post-access withdrawal: access pressure resolves through enactment while Ψ does not bind to the after-scene.
  • covert Ψ-expectation: non-binding language denies binding relevance that the scene helped structure.
  • after-scene dignity failure: the scene cannot be carried under Θ without degradation, shame residue, immunity, or self-worth leakage.
  • humiliation-to-control-collapse corridor: repeated humiliation-near marking overloads Χ/Ψ capacity.
  • sexed leniency drift: relief or blame tracks sex-coded readability instead of operator load.
  • asymmetric self-control burden: one role-position carries disproportionate Χ/Ψ demand without dignity recognition.
  • boundary-aggression collapse: boundary-setting and aggression become structurally unreadable.

Guard:
These overlays are configuration markers only. They do not diagnose persons, rank sexes, authorize violence, create entitlement, define orientation, establish maturity/adultness status, create a genital truth, or add a new operator. They remain subordinate to the canonical spine:

Δ → ∇ → □ → Λ → Α → Ω → Θ → Φ → Χ → Σ → Ψ

D.5 Minimal Viability Corridor (Overlay)

□ explicit
+ Ω nameable
+ Θ realistic
+ Χ operative
+ Λ tolerable
+ Ψ handled
(+ Σ reachable)
+ cost topology explicit
+ category pressure proportional
+ access non-entitled
+ body/boundary coding scene-bound
+ direct otherness non-entitled
+ genital meaning integrated / not sovereign
+ withdrawal expectations honestly carried
+ after-scene dignity intact
+ boundary/aggression distinguishable
+ asymmetry activation marked / bounded / re-bound
+ no parity-to-exit
+ no responsibility-to-authority
= structurally governable configuration

No moral claims.
No person labels.
No sex truths.
No maturity/adultness verdicts.
No practical instruction.
Only structural viability.

Viability increases where:

  • the frame remains legible,
  • asymmetry is named and governed,
  • temporality is treated as real,
  • non-events remain tolerable without becoming steering,
  • distance remains practically available,
  • self-binding is explicit, suspended, or kept out without leaking,
  • integration remains reachable where contradictions accumulate,
  • category pressure remains proportional,
  • access remains threshold-language rather than entitlement,
  • body/boundary coding remains scene-bound rather than person truth,
  • direct otherness remains reality-correction without access entitlement,
  • genital meaning remains integrated without genital sovereignty,
  • withdrawal carries structured Ψ-expectation honestly where it has become operative,
  • after-scene dignity remains intact,
  • self-control burdens remain visible as dignity-relevant costs,
  • boundary-setting remains distinguishable from aggression,
  • asymmetry activation remains marked, bounded, and re-bound.

Drift begins where:

  • frames narrow,
  • non-events steer,
  • attractors or categories monopolize,
  • asymmetry becomes leverage,
  • temporality is denied,
  • distance collapses,
  • labels erase outer form,
  • visible form is denied or totalized,
  • publicness is treated as either everything or nothing,
  • access simulation replaces concrete correction,
  • direct otherness is misread as access entitlement,
  • body/boundary coding becomes person truth,
  • genital meaning becomes genital sovereignty,
  • withdrawal disowns structured Ψ-expectation,
  • sexed leniency replaces operator reading,
  • one role-position carries disproportionate self-control burden without recognition,
  • boundary and aggression collapse into each other,
  • parity becomes exit,
  • responsibility becomes authority,
  • Ψ enters covertly.

D.6 Inner / Outer / Public Overlay

A scene may be:

  • internally framed one way,
  • externally readable another way,
  • publicly circulated in a third way,
  • and temporally carried in a fourth way.

PMS-SEX does not collapse these layers.

It reconstructs how frame, markedness, asymmetry, exposure, publicness, and consequence interact without allowing internal naming or public amplification to erase enacted form.

Internal framing
     ≠
Outer legibility
     ≠
Public circulation
     ≠
Temporal carryover

Guard:
Internal framing does not erase outer form.
Outer legibility does not authorize person-ranking.
Publicness may amplify what a scene becomes, but does not necessarily create what the scene already presents.

D.7 Publicness as Overlay

outer legibility
      ↓
publicness overlay
      ↓
amplification / documentation / repetition / sedimentation

Publicness may:

  • distribute readability,
  • amplify exposure,
  • document consequence,
  • repeat a scene beyond its original frame,
  • sedimentize reputation or stigma,
  • harden costs under Ω and Θ.

Publicness does not necessarily generate the primary action-form. Many configurations are already externally readable through asymmetry, exposure, markedness, bodily consequence, narrowed alternatives, or repeated action-form before public circulation occurs.

Two errors avoided:

  • reducing consequence to publicity alone,
  • ignoring publicity once documentation, circulation, or reputational sedimentation has entered the field.

D.9 Map Guardrails (Formal)

This map does not:

  • classify persons,
  • diagnose motives,
  • infer inner states,
  • rank identities,
  • create sexual-orientation taxonomy,
  • prescribe actions,
  • provide risk-management guidance,
  • justify public accusation,
  • replace legal, clinical, ethical, or MIP evaluation.

It answers one question only:

What does this configuration produce over time, under frame, non-event, repetition, asymmetry, temporality, and limited stop-capability?

D.10 Minimal Map Sentence (Citable)

PMS-SEX reads sexuality as a trajectory system: once difference is enacted under frames, non-events become active, repetition stabilizes paths, asymmetries distribute costs, time hardens consequences, and only operative distance can interrupt drift before self-binding captures the configuration.

D.11 Final One-Page Guard

No consequence-free sex.
No desire exempt from structural conditions.
No biology as destiny.
No dependency as relationship mandate.
No impulse-nearness collapsed into malice.
No lack of malice treated as consequence-free.
No direct otherness converted into access entitlement.
No outer-form erasure by internal labels.
No visible-form totalization.
No publicness reduction.
No path-cost as person-worth.
No category, access, body/boundary, or genital profile as person truth.
No genital meaning converted into genital sovereignty.
No withdrawal profile treated as sex essence.
No non-binding language used to erase structured Ψ-expectation.
No boundary-setting collapsed into aggression.
No aggression immunized as boundary-setting.
No critique through humiliation.
No maturity, adultness, or dignity verdict without explicit MIP docking.
No overlay term added to the operator spine.
No taxonomy where only configuration-language is warranted.
No political program, nostalgia, or liberation rhetoric where only macro-frame analysis is warranted.
No total capture where the scene exceeds the grammar.

PMS-SEX remains valid by staying within what it can responsibly say: not what persons are, but what configurations do over time. Its closing axis is: biology without destiny, dependency without mandate, impulse without malice-collapse, otherness without entitlement, genitality without sovereignty.
